  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_18786604-393f-41a5-9f45-83d69df5e952'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer3096726819855571172">1. The art is beautiful.<br/>2. The idea is WAAAAY original. I CAN'T FIND ANOTHER PLOT LIKE IT!!<br/>3. It teaches a valuable lesson that I ENCOURAGE MY REVIEW READERS TO FIND OUT FOR THEMSELVES. :)<br/><br/>Shugo Chara (NOTE: Pronounced Shoo-goh kah-rah! People have been calling it Shoo-goh cha-rah and I have the immediate urge to correct them! But I wouldn't know--I'm just a fan of pronouncing things the japanese way.) starts out as story about a young 4th grader (I can't believe how young they are...) named Amu </span>
  <span id="freeText3096726819855571172" style="display:none">1. The art is beautiful.<br />2. The idea is WAAAAY original. I CAN'T FIND ANOTHER PLOT LIKE IT!!<br />3. It teaches a valuable lesson that I ENCOURAGE MY REVIEW READERS TO FIND OUT FOR THEMSELVES. :)<br /><br />Shugo Chara (NOTE: Pronounced Shoo-goh kah-rah! People have been calling it Shoo-goh cha-rah and I have the immediate urge to correct them! But I wouldn't know--I'm just a fan of pronouncing things the japanese way.) starts out as story about a young 4th grader (I can't believe how young they are...) named Amu Hinamori.<br />Amu has been classified as a cool "Hot and spicy" type of girl, but deep down inside, she's an overreacting, excited girl. She dresses "punky and cool", but she's always wanted to wear something girly with lace. She has problems with showing her true feelings and emotions.<br />One night, she wishes that she would be able to show her true self to others, and the next morning, three small eggs appear in her room. This is where the plot begins to pick up.<br /><br />I started reading Shugo Chara when I was in the 6th grade, and I've only read up to volume nine--so nope, I'm not finished. But I want to review what I feel about this story so far, and I GIVE THIS STORY FOUR-STARS BECAUSE OF IT'S AWESOME BRILLIANCE!!!!!!!<br /><br />It's FOUR-STARS and not five-stars because Shugo Chara is a little too shoujo for me. But don't get me wrong--I love the plots and the art and the characters!<br /><br />I recommend this story for shoujo, mahou shoujo (magical girl) lovers! Now go read it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3096726819855571172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5386619-nina-s?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5386619-nina-s?shelf=magical-girl">magical-girl</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer882920001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3652828290668353100">I loved this. It was very cute and very sweet. Unfortunately though I'm only adding novels to my challenge this year, so I'm going to note her that I read it on the 14/03/2014-15/03/2014.<br/><br/><b>The plot: </b>Very straightforward, kind of predictable. But also has enough twists and turns to keep interested. Though it's like any usual shoujo manga. It's not like a mystery where you're suddenly thrown in another direction.<br/><br/><b>The Characters: </b> I loved Amu. I loved Ikuto. Amu is your usual Shoujo protag and yet she</span>
  <span id="freeText3652828290668353100" style="display:none">I loved this. It was very cute and very sweet. Unfortunately though I'm only adding novels to my challenge this year, so I'm going to note her that I read it on the 14/03/2014-15/03/2014.<br /><br /><b>The plot: </b>Very straightforward, kind of predictable. But also has enough twists and turns to keep interested. Though it's like any usual shoujo manga. It's not like a mystery where you're suddenly thrown in another direction.<br /><br /><b>The Characters: </b> I loved Amu. I loved Ikuto. Amu is your usual Shoujo protag and yet she wasn't. I liked her strong character, hated that she liked Tadase first, but then liked her again she realised later on that her feelings for Tadase were different. What I found weird and kind of oddly disturbing (though I got over this by pretending Amu was actually older) was that Amu is only an elementary school kid and yet Ikuto is a senior in highschool. The good thing was that there is no actual relationship between them except friendship and some hints about a possible relationship. The bad thing was, and this is why I didn't read it for so long: there is not actual relationship. Which on the plus side, means there's more of a focus on character and plot which is great!<br /><br /><b>The Magic: </b> I loved the heart eggs. I thought it was a good idea and totally ties the story with a very strong theme. And I liked it more I suppose because the protag is a child, so the theme works really well. Of course, genius, duh! I really, really love the idea of the hear eggs, you cannot imagine how much I love them. In fact they were my favourite part of the entire story!!<br /><br /><b>The Artwork and Writing:</b> All good, loved the artwork and the way the story was told was good. It was pretty easy to read. It was pretty to look at. <br /><br /><b>Overall:</b> What can I say? A very good magical girl story. I enjoyed it. Not as dark as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13110891.Puella_Magi_Madoka_Magica__Vol__01__Puella_Magi_Madoka_Magica___1_" title="Puella Magi Madoka Magica, Vol. 01 (Puella Magi Madoka Magica, #1) by Magica Quartet" rel="nofollow noopener">Puella Magi Madoka Magica, Vol. 01</a>, but also not light and fluffy with an overwhelming romance plot. It was fun!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3652828290668353100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899659-nick?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15225810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5721102489643982775"><b>Overall Rating: B+</b><br/><i>Synopsis: Created by Peach-Pit, the series is a shōjo manga that follows Amu Hinamori, a student at Seiyo Elementary. Amu has a reputation for being stylish and cool (that's her to the left), but she's really very shy. One night, she makes a wish that she could be her real self, and the next morning she finds three brightly colored eggs in her bed. Each egg eventually hatches a Guardian Character, angel-like beings able to change Amu into a new personality. She also has to deal</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5721102489643982775" style="display:none"><b>Overall Rating: B+</b><br /><i>Synopsis: Created by Peach-Pit, the series is a shōjo manga that follows Amu Hinamori, a student at Seiyo Elementary. Amu has a reputation for being stylish and cool (that's her to the left), but she's really very shy. One night, she makes a wish that she could be her real self, and the next morning she finds three brightly colored eggs in her bed. Each egg eventually hatches a Guardian Character, angel-like beings able to change Amu into a new personality. She also has to deal with the Guardians of Seiyo Elementary, a student council group who have their own Guardian Characters (and a really stupid looking cape). <br /><br />Of course, the current Guardian King at Seiyo (Guardians are based on cards, so you have King, Queen, Jack and Ace) is Tadase Hotori, Amu's love interest. As an example of how a Guardian Character can affect someone, whenever someone refers to Tadase as "Prince" (his nickname), he changes into a violent, egotistical king who wishes to rule the world. Fun, right?</i><br /><br />I grabbed the first volume of <i>Shugo Chara!</i>, because it looked ridiculously cute. So far, the first volume has delivered on that cuteness in spades. The plot is interesting and while it has some familiar aspects (for example, student council being treated like royalty, and the main character having mixed emotions about joining said council), I like the concept of Guardian Characters, and it's different enough to be intriguing. Hopefully the series will live up to its promise.<br /><br />For more manga and anime reviews, please check out <a href="http://hobotaku.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Hobotaku</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5721102489643982775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer562873340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13088950947131136117">Hinamori Amu is the most popular girl at Seiyo Elemantary school, known for her edgy fashion sense and "Cool-n-Spicy" attitude. Hell, even her own parents are huge fans of her. But in reality, Amu is just a scared girl who just wants to be cuter and more honest.<br/>Enter three eggs, who hatch into Guardian Characters, sort of mascots who represent who Amu wants to become. Ran represents her desire to more athletic and honest. Miki is her wish to be more artsy, and has her stubborn attitude. Suu is t</span>
  <span id="freeText13088950947131136117" style="display:none">Hinamori Amu is the most popular girl at Seiyo Elemantary school, known for her edgy fashion sense and "Cool-n-Spicy" attitude. Hell, even her own parents are huge fans of her. But in reality, Amu is just a scared girl who just wants to be cuter and more honest.<br />Enter three eggs, who hatch into Guardian Characters, sort of mascots who represent who Amu wants to become. Ran represents her desire to more athletic and honest. Miki is her wish to be more artsy, and has her stubborn attitude. Suu is the girliest of the three and is Amu's hopes to become more domestic.<br />Amu isn't the only one with Guardian Characters. There are also the Guardians, her school's student council who protect the happiness of the student body while also searching for a special egg called the Embryo, which is known to grant any wish. Among them are the childish Ace chair, Yuiki Yaya, the free spirit Jack chair, Souma Kukai, the refined Queen, Fujisaki Nadeshiko, and the popular yet kind King, Hotori Tadase.<br />But there's another group after the Embryo; a corrupt organization named Easter. Two of their workers also have Guardian characters. The stubborn idol Hoshina Utau and the reckless Ikuto, who may not actually be the enemy...<br />This is easily my favorite magical girl manga of all time. There are a whole bunch of characters that enter the story, and secrets revealed that you may not have seen coming.<br />Unless of course you go to the forums or blogs. But if you're looking to be surprised, be sure to look into this great series.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12164523817258598463">3.5*<br/><br/> I watched the anime first, so some of the terminology in the manga sounded peculiar to me. Especially "the self that I want to be", whereas the anime OP theme said "my would-be self". Also, the "Negative Heart, Lock-On!" that I loved so much in the anime, seems missing from the manga. Other than that, and how obvious it is that the mangakas are Amuto fangirls (which I despise, since I am a Tadamu fangirl), the manga is a decent read...even for those of us, who watched all of the anime first</span>
  <span id="freeText12164523817258598463" style="display:none">3.5*<br /><br /> I watched the anime first, so some of the terminology in the manga sounded peculiar to me. Especially "the self that I want to be", whereas the anime OP theme said "my would-be self". Also, the "Negative Heart, Lock-On!" that I loved so much in the anime, seems missing from the manga. Other than that, and how obvious it is that the mangakas are Amuto fangirls (which I despise, since I am a Tadamu fangirl), the manga is a decent read...even for those of us, who watched all of the anime first.<br /><br /> Regardless of the obvious pushing of the Amuto pairing in the manga, it is nice to see several instances of IkUtau and Tikuto in the manga as well....both of which are much better pairings than Amuto.<br /><br /> Also, it's sad that none of the Guardians--excluding Amu herself--can do the Character Transformations, yet, only the Character Change.</span>

<div id="review_2188406975" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2188406975" />
    <a title="~Cyanide Latte~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70514160-cyanide-latte"><img alt="~Cyanide Latte~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562894727p2/70514160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2188406975?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Cyanide Latte~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Cyanide Latte~" href="/user/show/70514160-cyanide-latte">~Cyanide Latte~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Mink, Dream Saga, Kamikaze Kaito Jeanne, and Full Moon o Sagashite</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70514160-cyanide-latte?shelf=manga-manhwa-manhua">manga-manhwa-manhua</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70514160-cyanide-latte?shelf=peach-pit-series">peach-pit-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2188406975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3514631391350095641">If you had to ask me what the likelihood was that I would find myself going back and trying out some of Peach-Pit's titles, up until recently, I would have laughed at you. If you had asked if I would read <i>Shugo Chara!</i> in particular, I probably would have snorted as well. I used to be of the opinion that a lot of Peach-Pit's work was overrated and overhyped, and to some degree when I think back on high school, I still think they're somewhat overhyped or at least were.<br/><br/>But I picked up this copy of </span>
  <span id="freeText3514631391350095641" style="display:none">If you had to ask me what the likelihood was that I would find myself going back and trying out some of Peach-Pit's titles, up until recently, I would have laughed at you. If you had asked if I would read <i>Shugo Chara!</i> in particular, I probably would have snorted as well. I used to be of the opinion that a lot of Peach-Pit's work was overrated and overhyped, and to some degree when I think back on high school, I still think they're somewhat overhyped or at least were.<br /><br />But I picked up this copy of the first volume on a whim and decided I might as well give it a shot. I've been in the mood for fluffy shoujo to sort of balance out a lot of the intense tones of the novels I've been reading, and I do have to say that this delivered beyond my expectations. I had initially thought <i>Shugo Chara!</i> would just be slice-of-life with some magical realism, but this volume surprised me, as there is evidently a much greater plot in store beyond just the one described in the summary.<br /><br />So what <i>is</i> series about? We have our main character Amu, who comes across as a cold and aloof mini punk-goth (not helped by her mother selecting her clothes,) but has a major case of shyness and a tendency to speak bluntly. When ruminating over her desire to be able to show more of her inner self, she awakes the following morning to find three decorative eggs that, over the course of this volume, hatch "Guardian Characters" that enable her to act out or bring forth aspects of herself she typically keeps hidden. We get as much from the volume's summary.<br /><br />In addition to that, we also learn she isn't the only person who has Guardian Characters, and there are several other people with Guardian Characters on the hunt for something in particular. I won't say much more beyond that, as it will definitely get into some serious spoiler territory.<br /><br />But for what it's worth, the fact that there was more to the story and its plot pleasantly surprised me, and I definitely am looking forward to eventually reading more of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3514631391350095641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1146478130" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1146478130" />
    <a title="Maeve K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24217513-maeve-k"><img alt="Maeve K." src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1146478130?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maeve K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maeve K." href="/user/show/24217513-maeve-k">Maeve K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1146478130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18235420714622827393">Shugo Chara: Volume 1 was written by Peach-Pit a female manga artist duo consisting of Banri Sendo and Shibuko Ebara. It was published in Japan on January 1st, 2006 by Kodansha Ltd., Tokyo. Since this manga/graphic novel was originally written in Japanese, it was translated into english by June Kato. This graphic novel falls into the genre of Magical Girl. This genre is a subgenre of Japanese fantasy manga as well as anime that feature young girls who are, of course, using magic. If you’re think</span>
  <span id="freeText18235420714622827393" style="display:none">Shugo Chara: Volume 1 was written by Peach-Pit a female manga artist duo consisting of Banri Sendo and Shibuko Ebara. It was published in Japan on January 1st, 2006 by Kodansha Ltd., Tokyo. Since this manga/graphic novel was originally written in Japanese, it was translated into english by June Kato. This graphic novel falls into the genre of Magical Girl. This genre is a subgenre of Japanese fantasy manga as well as anime that feature young girls who are, of course, using magic. If you’re thinking, “This genre doesn’t exist!, it does in Japan. It is also referred to as a shojo manga, meaning it was written to market towards female readers between the ages of 10 and 18. <br /><br />This story is about a 4th grade girl, Amu Hinamori, who is considered “cool” and “spicy” by her entire school, Seiyo Elementary. Due to this, she feels as if its too late to be who she really is inside, her true self. One morning, after Amu wished to be able to be who she really is, she wakes up to find three strange, colored, little eggs under her sheets. Contained each egg is a Guardian Character. Every child has one and their objective is to help children be who they really are. Although, the main antagonists are a company called Easter who search and destroy children’s Guardian Characters. The reason they do this is their goal is to retrieve a specific egg called the Embryo which has the power to make one person's wish come true. Join her through a world of magic and a mysterious teenage boy as she learns more about theses so called Charas (Guardian Characters). With the help of her Guardian Characters and her friends, the Guardians who have Charas as well, Amu will learn her true self shocking.<br /><br />The metacognitive strategy that I found helpful is making connections because I can relate to the main character, Amu. When making a connection, you use what you know to make a connection to the text you are reading. To show how I connect with the character, I chose these quotes from a scene Amu is sitting on her bed thinking about how she acts at school and when her fake self takes over. <br />“‘I’m tired of being that exterior character I am on the outside!” (22)<br />In addition,<br />“My exterior character has a life of its own… I want to feel cute and be who I really am. But I can’t be like that now. Because that’s not my true character.” (23)<br /><br />This is a connection for me because I try to be a non extreme tomboy, saying how I hate pink, sparkles and ruffles when inside I’m not an uber tomboy and that I’m actually quite girly inside. When someone brings up that they don’t like a band or they don’t like a character in a series and other people agree, I immediately agree as well even when my opinion is just a lie. I do this to fit in more and when I finally gather the courage to announce my real opinion, I feel like it would mess everything up because people already know that I don’t like this and I like this and that it would be too late. This is why I chose these quotes for my connection.<br />	<br />I think that this book has a great message for girls, since it is a shojo manga, especially in the teenage years when girls start to feel the need to change how they are just to fit in, to be yourself. Because sometimes when you try to be someone you're not you can mess things up. The scene I chose to show this is where Amu arrives at school and the Guardians of the school, meaning they just do anything a guardian does a anyone and they all have Guardian Charas, are there. Since there are different chairs, meaning positions, Tadase Hotori, Kings chair, approaches Amu when he senses that she also has Charas. When he grabs her, her exterior character acts on it, slapping his hand away from her.<br />	“‘Don’t touch me without my permission. Mr. Little Boy.’<br />	‘Ah… I’m sorry.’” (33)<br />In addition, after the interaction with Tadase, she moves out of view, slumping to the ground, saying,<br />“‘I did it again! I’m such an idiot! I’m so phony! I’ve been dreaming of our first meeting and I ruined it!!’” (33)<br />This evidence shows that when her exterior character acted upon this interaction, she had the possible chance of messing up her first meeting with her long lasting crush and a new friend. This relates to teenage girls because in the teenage world, when you act differently to other people, you could mess up your friendships because your friends don’t like the fake you and they like the real you. Also, people could get the the wrong impression from you when you say something that you don’t mean. Something that you think is cool but really isn’t. This is why I think that this book, well series, has a fantastic message for teen girls. This is really a great story and I highly recommend it. That is if you’re a teen girl or if you’re just into these kind of stories.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18235420714622827393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer78954842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1825921685234388153">My review will be on the original non-edited version that some kind people translate for us on the internet cos Del Rey suck (no offence to you guys and all) and 'edit' (or as I like to say, make loads of mistake in) the translation... WHICH IS REALLY, REALLY ANNOYING!!! Seriously annoying... seriously, seriously annoying... you don't know how long I can rant about something like that cos I appreciate the Japanese culture and language so much... (speaking of which, anyone wanna lend me £1000 so </span>
  <span id="freeText1825921685234388153" style="display:none">My review will be on the original non-edited version that some kind people translate for us on the internet cos Del Rey suck (no offence to you guys and all) and 'edit' (or as I like to say, make loads of mistake in) the translation... WHICH IS REALLY, REALLY ANNOYING!!! Seriously annoying... seriously, seriously annoying... you don't know how long I can rant about something like that cos I appreciate the Japanese culture and language so much... (speaking of which, anyone wanna lend me £1000 so I can go there?)<br /><br />The story focuses on the life of Hinamori Amu (or Amu Hinamori if you prefer the english term...) who is respected and known for her 'cool and spicy' exterior self. However, deep down Amu is just a shy, quiet girl (like me) who finds it a bit (VERY) hard to be honest and express her feelings... (OMG! WE'RE TWINS!!! Apart from the cool and spicy part... but I'm not a nerd, geek, etc either... just normal XD)... EVEN HER PARENTS THINK SHE'S 'COOL AND SPICY!!!'<br />One day, after (being forced to) watch a fat psychic woman go on about Guardian Characters on the TV she goes to her room and wishes that she could be a more open, honest girl (or something like that... it's been like a year ever since I read Chapter 1 people! I'm on Vol.10, Ch.46...)<br />So if by magic, the next day, she finds some brightly coloured and patterned eggs on her bed... then she starts to panic as all partially sane people would if they found out they had just 'layed' an egg...<br />Of course, I haven't told you about the guy Amu likes yet, mostly cos I HATE HATE HATE him until he apologizes and learns to work together with my 2nd favourite character... (Utau's my first!!!) but she has a crush on Hotori Tadase (Tadase Hotori) aka the prince of the school... he belongs to something sorta like a school council which are the 'Guardians' or the school... In this belongs Tadase (King chair), Fujisaki Nadeshiko (Queen's chair - who is later replaced), Sohma Kuukai (Jack's chair - who is later replaced when he graduates... *sob*) and Yuiki Yaya (Ace Chair). Like Amu, they all have guardian characters too! So once they spot her guardian characters, <b>BANG</b>, she's part of them (mostly cos she's an idiot and can't say no to the stupid kiddy king who turns not so stupid around chapter 35ish...)!!!<br />I also forgot to mention Amu's Shugo Chara are Ran (who's symbol is the heart) who's very sporty, Miki (spade) who's very artistic and Suu (Club/Clover) who has amazing domestic skills!!! (Later on she also gets another character who you can probably work out by yourself...)... Now if you don't see the connection betweeen all of this READ THE ENTIRE REVIEW AGAIN UNTIL YOU DO!!!<br /><b>I'm getting tired now, so I'll just introduce a few more main characters before you go off to mangafox.com to read it... or you can buy it which Peach-Pit will appreciate, read it then read the one on the internet cos it's tons better than the Del Rey one!!!</b><br />There's Tsukiyomi Ikuto, another one of Amu's love interests and my 2nd fave character... you can have your own view on him but he is pure awesomenss and as Phoebe and Philippa (my BFFs) would say 'Well fit!!!'.<br />Also there's Hoshina Utau... don't judge her right away cos that's not what she's truly like and she's not really evil... just looking out for a certain someone... (but I still support Amu X Ikuto!!!)<br />There's also the replacements for the guardians who resign but I don't want to completely spoil the story...<br />And there's also the big bad evil (not really but still...) company who crush people's dreams so they can get the 'Embryo' (not explaining, go read the manga already...) for their boss, known as 'Gozen'...<br /><br />So yeah, 10/10 for Art, 9.5/10 for characters and 9/10 for story!!!</span>

<div id="review_53348693" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53348693" />
    <a title="Rems" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2237262-rems"><img alt="Rems" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459169550p2/2237262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53348693?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rems" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rems" href="/user/show/2237262-rems">Rems</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2237262-rems?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2237262-rems?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53348693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12997966699586010994">Ah, Shugo Chara!. This is a series which really does break away from the boundaries and conventions of its preordained genre and give you something new for the audience. It takes the stereotypical aspects of <i>mahou shoujo</i>, of course, but it runs with them - uses some more than others and disregards some of the more cliché ones. It's not all about the sparkles and the saving the world and the impossibly comfortable outfits and impossible hair colours and so forth. Okay, it is about all of that, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText12997966699586010994" style="display:none">Ah, Shugo Chara!. This is a series which really does break away from the boundaries and conventions of its preordained genre and give you something new for the audience. It takes the stereotypical aspects of <i>mahou shoujo</i>, of course, but it runs with them - uses some more than others and disregards some of the more cliché ones. It's not all about the sparkles and the saving the world and the impossibly comfortable outfits and impossible hair colours and so forth. Okay, it is about all of that, but not to horrific, endearing degrees. Most of all, to me, it's about a group of characters with real problems as they step into teendom and independance and learn to find their true selves.<br /><br />First, let's face it - how many times have you questioned who you are? Questioned your <i>true</i> self? Probably a fair few. I know I have. That was probably one of my lures to the series. It really is something that most anyone can relate to. <br /><br />Amu Hinamori feels outcast from the rest of her class - to them, she plays her false persona, a 'cool and spicy' girl who is too endearingly cool to approach, and has everyone under her thumb, and never looses pace, and so forth. The truth is she doesn't feel that way at all - that's not who she is on the inside, which is a stubbornly caring cool yet kindhearted girl who just wants to be accepted and be true to herself. So, she wishes - and the next day three eggs, which turn out to be her very own guardian characters (Shugo Chara) appear before her, which leads to her being drafted into the Guardians, and then join in the mission to effectively get hold of the Embyro and stop a company named Easter from destroying the souls of children and erasing their dreams.<br /><br />However, it's not all about Amu. Which, even though I love her dearly, is a strong selling point. It is very, very difficult to hate any character in this series for any given length of time. They're not 2-dimensional - they're fleshed out and given histories, backgrounds, real life problems, such as parents who fight over work and younger siblings taking over your limelight and so forth. True, you may not be a fan of every character, but there will definately be one that reaches out and calls to you after the series breaks through their false personalties to the raw character underneath. Ikuto also gets a mention because hey, Ikuto.<br /><br />And as it goes further on, it's just a really touching series that has messages behind it, and is a wonderful read. Fully reccommend you to keep reading to the currently translated volumes and beyond.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12997966699586010994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_272775042" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272775042" />
    <a title="Hermione" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7630060-hermione"><img alt="Hermione" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404088619p2/7630060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272775042?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hermione" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hermione" href="/user/show/7630060-hermione">Hermione</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7630060-hermione?shelf=delicious-boys">delicious-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7630060-hermione?shelf=girls-who-can-kick-my-ass">girls-who-can-kick-my-ass</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7630060-hermione?shelf=paranormal-or-fantasy-or-magic">paranormal-or-fantasy-or-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7630060-hermione?shelf=totally-did-not-see-that-coming">totally-did-not-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7630060-hermione?shelf=memorable">memorable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7630060-hermione?shelf=because-of-the-hype">because-of-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7630060-hermione?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7630060-hermione?shelf=forever-in-my-heart">forever-in-my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7630060-hermione?shelf=tv-or-movie-adaption">tv-or-movie-adaption</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272775042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15159076236338688925"><i>This review will be for the whole series.</i><br/><br/>When I finished the official last chapter of Shugo Chara! back in 2010, I was an emotional wreck. Some people don't understand; I was <i>obsessed</i> with this series. The idea was original, the characters pleasant and adorable, the plot perfect with just the right amount of dark/light elements.<br/><br/> I was devastated when it ended. <br/><br/>Granted, I probably hadn't stuck to it for no more than a year and a half. I found out about it around the summer of 2009, and it ended w</span>
  <span id="freeText15159076236338688925" style="display:none"><i>This review will be for the whole series.</i><br /><br />When I finished the official last chapter of Shugo Chara! back in 2010, I was an emotional wreck. Some people don't understand; I was <i>obsessed</i> with this series. The idea was original, the characters pleasant and adorable, the plot perfect with just the right amount of dark/light elements.<br /><br /> I was devastated when it ended. <br /><br />Granted, I probably hadn't stuck to it for no more than a year and a half. I found out about it around the summer of 2009, and it ended with the Encore chapters around spring 2010. But hell, it was beautiful, it was lovely, it was memorable. I totally adored the idea and all the unique elements to it. Every character kept surprising me. Hell, <i>Amu</i> kept surprising me. I cried, I laughed, I fumed, I had fangirl-giggly moments. I experienced so many emotions reading this. And while a part of me knew that this series was going to end, I kept it pushed back to the farthest of my mind. I enjoyed the brief moments we got an insight into everyone's thoughts. I also enjoyed how our "dark, brooding, mysterious" Tsukiyomi Ikuto wasn't just like because Peach-Pit made him to attract fangirls. His reasons for being who he was were amazingly crafted and so realistic. Amu's reasons for being insecure were rightfully challenged. <i>Everything</i> about this manga was beautiful. <br /><br />In conclusion, there are probably no words or gifs to describe how I felt about this manga. Each character evoked such heartwrenching emotions from the pits of my heart. All in all, this whole series was about growth and finding one's true self. We saw that. We saw the growth in Amu and in Ikuto and in Tadase. We saw the growth in each one of these characters. The growth was so big that, comparing their previous selves vs. their present selves, made me cry with such bittersweetness -- because they were growing. They grew, they surpassed all their trials and achieved each of their respective endings to their respective stories. <br /><br />My only regret? That I was not able to find out about this series sooner. <br /><br /><b>Five billion stars out of five billions stars.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15159076236338688925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_135074153" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer17998317540054090037">Review #15 ~I think~ ) This is one of the best manga I've read. I love the story plot so far and I also love the pictures...   <span id="freeText17998317540054090037" style="display:none">Review #15 ~I think~ ) This is one of the best manga I've read. I love the story plot so far and I also love the pictures... The pictures are detailed and very cute. The main character,fourth grader Amu, doesn't like the ways she acts, or how she fits into the community. People see Amu as the cool punk girl because of the clothing she wears( that her mother bought her). Her personality is nothing like that though. So one night, Amu wished so bad that she could "start over." The next morning, thinking she gave "birth" to them, she found three eggs on her bed. Not knowing what they were, she took them to school. When she gets to school she meets the "Prince", Tadase Hotori, and she falls in love with him right away. The "Prince" goes up to her and seems to realize that she has "the eggs." Surprised, she slaps his hand from reaching her. Everyone was surprised in what she did. She regretted it. During the Guardian, "something changed her character." In the middle of the meeting, she "character changed." In other words, her personality changed. She had confessed her love head-on. Embarrassed, she ran away from the meeting.<br /><br />While running, she wishes that she would fall in a hole... Which she does... She falls down a man-hole, landing safely on the ground. There she finds a guy who wants her (character) eggs. He steals one of them and then trouble kicks in. They are both about to be buried alive when the stolen egg hatched and "thing" (Guardian Character) flew Amu out of the hole. The other guy (Ikuto) got out himself with his Guardian Character. <br /><br />Later on in the story, the Guardian members are recruiting new members. In which they chose Amu (because she had three Guardian Characters). Amu declines but the Guardian members don't give up too easily. In the end, they get her to join... (They kind of forced her actually...).<br /><br />In the end of this volume, Amu cooks for Tadase, she meets up with Ikuto again, and she finds out about her job.<br /><br />This book is filled with fantasy and it also related to our community theme. I give it five stars!</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6653233-lena-nguyen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295157541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11687840107425907428">This manga was very unique in its storyline as well as the art. The art was really top notch, as expected of the duo, PEACH-PIT. The story itself was like no other, and that's saying something because nowadays, you see the same things repeating itself over and over again, so this was a fresh start and it truly set itself apart from all of that. This manga was very empowering, because I remembered that during the time when I read this, I was going through a difficult time in my life and I couldn'</span>
  <span id="freeText11687840107425907428" style="display:none">This manga was very unique in its storyline as well as the art. The art was really top notch, as expected of the duo, PEACH-PIT. The story itself was like no other, and that's saying something because nowadays, you see the same things repeating itself over and over again, so this was a fresh start and it truly set itself apart from all of that. This manga was very empowering, because I remembered that during the time when I read this, I was going through a difficult time in my life and I couldn't fit in with anyone at school. I couldn't find myself, in a manner of speaking. It was just a lot of social issues about who I should hang out with because of pressure and who I want to hang out with. I was in the eight grade, so this was a lot to deal with. It was just very difficult, and that was why I was so compelled by this manga and its heroine, Hinamori Amu. The heroine of this manga is completely different than many from the shoujo genre. Where most of the heroines are shy, clumsy, kind, adorable, and a complete DITZ, Amu is actually shy but hides herself by acting tough and cold. Lots of humor happens because of this. She also has the tendency to be a hothead and talk back to people instead of submitting herself or cry or whatever it is most typical shoujo heroines do. She's just a badass fourth grader, simply put, but a very kind one too. This manga is more than just a manga. It saved me because it speaks to those who are unsure of themselves and wish to become who they want to be. It has a very motivational message towards younger kids. THIS MANGA ACTUALLY HAS A POSITIVE MESSAGE!! Most shoujo mangas are overload with messages of lust jealousy and sex all that, but there isn't a trace of that here. It's something a growing preteen/teen should read while they're at that "awkward and experimental growing stage" where they like to experiment with different looks and being with different people and trying to get comfortable with themselves. A great manga and a great series! The anime sucks in my opinion because there are too many fillers, but the manga is great!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11687840107425907428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7963521699925119580">Shugo Chara vol.1<br/>Peach Pit, Shugo Chara, Kondasha publishing’s, 2007, 200p<br/> Have you ever felt like someone that you’re not and just keep acting like it? And you just wished that you can change yourself? That’s how Hinamori Amu feels in the cute little manga made by Peach Pit. This is one of the cutest manga I have read in my entire life, it’s just so darn adorable it will make your teeth rot I swear. Now join me as I tell Amu’s story as it starts out with three little eggs.<br/> Taking place in Tokyo</span>
  <span id="freeText7963521699925119580" style="display:none">Shugo Chara vol.1<br />Peach Pit, Shugo Chara, Kondasha publishing’s, 2007, 200p<br /> Have you ever felt like someone that you’re not and just keep acting like it? And you just wished that you can change yourself? That’s how Hinamori Amu feels in the cute little manga made by Peach Pit. This is one of the cutest manga I have read in my entire life, it’s just so darn adorable it will make your teeth rot I swear. Now join me as I tell Amu’s story as it starts out with three little eggs.<br /> Taking place in Tokyo Japan, at Seiyo Elementary which Hinamori Amu is a 5th grade student in the star class. Her classmates see her as ‘cool and spicy’ since at school she has that tough girl look and doesn’t care for cutesy things and some rumors speculate about her personal life. But Amu is actually a really shy girl who actually loves cute things; the rumors of her personal life are just a big fat lie. But she doesn’t have the guts to tell everyone that, she doesn’t want everyone to think of her as a weakling so one night she prays for herself to change; to be courageous artistic and talented. But the next day when she woke up she saw that she actually laid a red, blue, and green egg that later hatched into Ran, Miki, and Su who are actually her would be self. Soon the school guardians who also have charas (would be self) recruit Amu as their ‘joker’ to purify the x eggs and x characters who come from someone’s corrupted dreams. But it’s not going to be easy since a company named Easter is the cause of all this, just because their looking for the Embryo which can grant any wish. Will Amu and the others get to it before they do?<br /> Peach pit did an amazing job writing this series of 11 books. I just thought the idea of the little fairies as there would be self was so cute. I just love reading this series. I kind of feel like Amu does…..this is a great fantasy graphic novel…..I would recommend it to any fantasy manga lovers………….CIAO! <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1446396208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1446396208" />
    <a title="Conan Tigard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48525684-conan-tigard"><img alt="Conan Tigard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446528214p2/48525684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1446396208?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Conan Tigard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Conan Tigard" href="/user/show/48525684-conan-tigard">Conan Tigard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1446396208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16002775424580608851">Shugo Chara!: Volume 1 is a fun, little manga book about students with Guardian Characters that let them transform into different people. Well, not different people . . . they are still the same person. But when they change, each person has different talents. The Guardians have been waiting for for a person with three Guardian Characters to fill the "Joker" seat. The Joker Guardian has a job to do . They have to go out and find X Eggs before they hatch. X Eggs contain X Characters, which are the</span>
  <span id="freeText16002775424580608851" style="display:none">Shugo Chara!: Volume 1 is a fun, little manga book about students with Guardian Characters that let them transform into different people. Well, not different people . . . they are still the same person. But when they change, each person has different talents. The Guardians have been waiting for for a person with three Guardian Characters to fill the "Joker" seat. The Joker Guardian has a job to do . They have to go out and find X Eggs before they hatch. X Eggs contain X Characters, which are the bad versions of Guardian Characters and turn the owner bad. <br /><br />You know, at first, just from the cover and glancing at the first few pages, I didn't want to read this book very much because I thought it was going to be one those cutesy-tootsie mangas. But I'll tell you what, I had a great time reading it. The concept is pretty cool and I really enjoyed meeting all of the main characters for the first time. <br /><br />Sure, Amu is a little wishy-washy, but I really liked her. I bet she will get it all together soon. The bad guys, which we haven't met all of them yet, are pretty cool. I am really interested to see if the "Embryo" will show up soon, and who will get it. <br /><br />As for the artwork, it is really terrific. The Translation and Adaptation is also pretty good. No complaints. <br /><br />Overall, Shugo Chara!: Volume 1 is a great manga book and a wonderful beginning to a new series. I wonder if Amu will be able to capture and seal the X Egg before it hatches in Shugo Chara!: Volume 2. Let's hope so.<br /><br />I rated this book an 8 out of 10.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16002775424580608851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16619807090220596904">Everybody at school thinks Amu is amazing. They want to be her and they idolize her, because she's so tough. Amu is struggling with her image, because it isn't who she really is. She is a sweet girl who wants to wear cute things. Amu wishes she can be herself.   <span id="freeText16619807090220596904" style="display:none">Everybody at school thinks Amu is amazing. They want to be her and they idolize her, because she's so tough. Amu is struggling with her image, because it isn't who she really is. She is a sweet girl who wants to wear cute things. Amu wishes she can be herself. With the help of a bit of magic three eggs are the result. At first Amu has no idea what they are for, but soon she finds out that each egg contains a Guardian Character. These characters are her would be selves. With the help of her three eggs Amu can be who she wants to be. The Guardian Characters are changing Amu's life. Are they only a blessing for Amu and what happens when she learns to use her new abilities? <br /><br />Shugo Chara! is the first manga I've ever read. I was instantly hooked and read the story in one go. I loved it. The drawings are beautiful and the story is great. Aren't we all insecure when we go to school, even the most popular people? The idea of the magic and the three eggs instantly appealed to me. I enjoyed reading this volume immensely and am definitely going to read the second part as well. This isn't a stand alone story, it's part of a series. There are several fabulous girls, a handsome prince and some good kicking and screaming. These ingredients together are making a fabulous story. I really like the cover, the pink hair is great. Shugo Chara! has gotten me hooked, I've already purchased several other manga books for my kindle.</span>

<div id="review_154517078" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154517078" />
    <a title="Lex Mori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4858364-lex-mori"><img alt="Lex Mori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473745206p2/4858364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154517078?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lex Mori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lex Mori" href="/user/show/4858364-lex-mori">Lex Mori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858364-lex-mori?shelf=great-not-favorite">great-not-favorite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154517078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7456917709561309350">This adorable story with cute characters and a mysterious plot is definitely different from most manga out there. Following elementary student and accidentally acclaimed badass, Amu Hinamori, we learn about the Shugo Chara, or "Guardian Characters" and their roles in the world of this story.<br/>The pace was slower in general, but it was the perfect pace for this story. The plot is different and always tries to keep you guessing. The artwork is great with lots of attention to detail. The characters a</span>
  <span id="freeText7456917709561309350" style="display:none">This adorable story with cute characters and a mysterious plot is definitely different from most manga out there. Following elementary student and accidentally acclaimed badass, Amu Hinamori, we learn about the Shugo Chara, or "Guardian Characters" and their roles in the world of this story.<br />The pace was slower in general, but it was the perfect pace for this story. The plot is different and always tries to keep you guessing. The artwork is great with lots of attention to detail. The characters are adorable. Overall, my only complaint is that there are some suggestive themes that would not have been a big problem had the characters not been in the 4th to 6th grade. One particular outfit Amu wears had me worried. Had these characters been older or at least into their teens, it wouldn't have been such a big deal. But luckily, these themes are few and far between and are only worthy of a side note.<br />Overall, too cute, good story, good demographic. I would probably leave this to a younger crowd, (yes, despite the bits I just mentioned), but I might check out the next volume just to see what happens.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7456917709561309350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3354044100817428174">Shugo chara is one of those books when I could feel like reading it any time of the day, it is always funny, sometimes serious or lovey dovey or totally complicated. I agree to those people who say it's "kinda childish" or "makes no sense" or people who say that the plot is not the best that they've seen or something like that. I totally agree to that, I actually really liked it at first and hated it after I finished reading it but I liked it again after I realised that it's not too bad and it's</span>
  <span id="freeText3354044100817428174" style="display:none">Shugo chara is one of those books when I could feel like reading it any time of the day, it is always funny, sometimes serious or lovey dovey or totally complicated. I agree to those people who say it's "kinda childish" or "makes no sense" or people who say that the plot is not the best that they've seen or something like that. I totally agree to that, I actually really liked it at first and hated it after I finished reading it but I liked it again after I realised that it's not too bad and it's like once in a while you get to hear a manga with this type of story. I will definitely recommend this to anyone who likes reading funny mangas, because of the awesome illustrations and the comedy in this series. <br /><br />If you find the first volume a bit bad then give it another go and try the next volume because i find Shugo Chara really good but I do agree that it's not my most favourite but it is one of my favourites.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zohal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zohal" href="/user/show/4035082-zohal">Zohal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4035082-zohal?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4035082-zohal?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4035082-zohal?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4035082-zohal?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116966902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14323149297518366">While this is an irresistibly cute manga, don't be fooled by the overly cutesy character design because the female lead has more than enough charm and personality to win over both male and female readers. I watched the anime first and loved it due to the lovable main character, beautiful art/attractive character deigns, and simple yet sweet premise and so far the manga definitely feels like it's worth the read. It's genuinely funny (it made me laugh out loud at times) and even though the general</span>
  <span id="freeText14323149297518366" style="display:none">While this is an irresistibly cute manga, don't be fooled by the overly cutesy character design because the female lead has more than enough charm and personality to win over both male and female readers. I watched the anime first and loved it due to the lovable main character, beautiful art/attractive character deigns, and simple yet sweet premise and so far the manga definitely feels like it's worth the read. It's genuinely funny (it made me laugh out loud at times) and even though the general plot and concepts (such as costumed kids gifted with the magical power to unlock their hearts in order to resurrect hearts gone bad...yeah, seriously) sound so corny in theory, the overall package is handled so maturely that no shame is felt in being reeled in by such a well-meaning story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14323149297518366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wLihorO1inc2ZWwlvmOKVf7ifXPiuLLlDb3Exw2Xnuaq09PGpvILULe6UDIW/xdAKSuwB559Yg4/o3haAgrZSg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8775257148295283147">Peach-Pit (ピーチ・ピット Pīchi Pitto) is a female manga artist duo in Japan, made up of Banri Sendo (千道 万里 Sendō Banri) and Shibuko Ebara (えばら 渋子 Ebara Shibuko). Their group name derives from the diner hangout Peach-Pit from the TV show Beverly Hills, 90210. Although both have similar styles, with some artwork it is possible to identify which artist drew it. Both are known for their bishōjo styled works</span>
  <span id="freeText8775257148295283147" style="display:none">Peach-Pit (ピーチ・ピット Pīchi Pitto) is a female manga artist duo in Japan, made up of Banri Sendo (千道 万里 Sendō Banri) and Shibuko Ebara (えばら 渋子 Ebara Shibuko). Their group name derives from the diner hangout Peach-Pit from the TV show Beverly Hills, 90210. Although both have similar styles, with some artwork it is possible to identify which artist drew it. Both are known for their bishōjo styled works. As noted in their books, they are both Geminis and have "Almost flushed our phones down the toilet...twice."<br /><br />The two of them grew up together and went to the same elementary school and have been best friends ever since. Both started as doujinshi manga artists, but not as Peach-Pit. Then they were scouted by Dengeki Comic Gao!. In 2008, one of their manga, Shugo Chara!, was awarded the Kodansha Manga Award for best children's manga. Shugo Chara was also turned later into an Anime television series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8775257148295283147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
